(2019)</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><table class="infobox-subbox"><tbody><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Passengers</th><td class="infobox-data">26,360,003</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Freight (<a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">tonnes</a>)</th><td class="infobox-data">500,702</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Aircraft movements</th><td class="infobox-data">234,460</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Sources: Brussels Airport,<sup id="cite_ref-stats_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Belgian <a href="/wiki/Aeronautical_Information_Publication" title="Aeronautical Information Publication">AIP</a><sup id="cite_ref-aip_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Brussels Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>BRU</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>EBBR</b>) (also called <i><i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">Brussel-Nationaal</i></i> / <i><i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Bruxelles-National</i></i> (Brussels-National) or <i>Luchthaven Zaventem</i>) is an <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> 6.5&#160;<a href="/wiki/Nautical_mile" title="Nautical mile">NM</a> (12.0&#160;km; 7.5&#160;mi) northeast<sup id="cite_ref-aip_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> of <a href="/wiki/City_of_Brussels" title="City of Brussels">Brussels</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Capital_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels Capital Region">capital</a> of <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>. In 2019, more than 26 million passengers arrived or departed at Brussels Airport, making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">24th busiest airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>. It is located in the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Zaventem" title="Zaventem">Zaventem</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Brabant" title="Flemish Brabant">Province of Flemish Brabant</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Region" title="Flemish Region">Flemish Region</a> of <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>. It is home to around 260 companies, together directly employing 20,000 people and serves as the home base for <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airlines" title="Brussels Airlines">Brussels Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/TUI_fly_Belgium" title="TUI fly Belgium">TUI fly Belgium</a>.\n</p><p>The company operating the airport is known as The Brussels Airport Company N.V./S.A.; before 19 October 2006, the name was BIAC (Brussels International Airport Company), which was created by Belgian law through a merger of BATC with the ground operations departments of the RLW/RVA. Since 2011, the airport has been owned by the <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Ontario_Teachers%27_Pension_Plan" title="Ontario Teachers&#39; Pension Plan">Ontario Teachers\' Pension Plan</a> (39%), <a href="/wiki/Macquarie_Group" title="Macquarie Group">Macquarie Group</a> (Macquarie European Infrastructure Fund I and Macquarie European Infrastructure Fund III) (36%) and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Government_of_Belgium" title="Federal Government of Belgium">Belgian State</a> (25%).<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 22 March 2016, the airport\'s departures hall was severely damaged by <a href="/wiki/2016_Brussels_bombings" title="2016 Brussels bombings">two terrorist bomb blasts</a>. The airport was closed until 3 April 2016, when it was reopened with temporary facilities at less than 20% of its previous capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg.com_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg.com-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> It has since returned to full operations, with a record of 90,000 passengers on 29 July 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The origins of Brussels Airport at Zaventem date back to 1940, when the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">German</a> occupying force claimed 600&#160;ha (1,500 acres) of agricultural fields reserved as a back-up airfield ("Steenokkerzeel"). There the <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a> established <b>Fliegerhorst Melsbroek</b> and constructed 3 <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runways</a> in the shape of a triangle: runway 02/20, runway 07L/25R (both of which are still in use today) and runway 12/30. The airport buildings were constructed in the nearby municipality of Melsbroek and not of Zaventem, which is why the airfield was known to the locals as Melsbroek (in Dutch) (or "Fliegerhorst Melsbroek" in German). There is an <a href="/wiki/Urban_legend" title="Urban legend">urban legend</a> that the site of the airport was chosen by the Germans after asking locals where to build it\xe2\x80\x93the Belgians then pointed to this location as it was often foggy.\n</p><p>After the liberation on 3 September 1944, the German infrastructure at Melsbroek fell into the hands of the British. When the <a href="/wiki/Evere_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Evere Airport">old civilian airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Haren,_Belgium" title="Haren, Belgium">Haren</a> became too small, the Belgian authorities decided to use the aerodrome at Melsbroek for the new national airport. By 1948, a new <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">terminal</a> building was constructed to replace the old wooden building. In the same year, the lengths of both runways 02/20 and 07L/25R were increased, to 1,200&#160;m (3,900&#160;ft) and 2,450&#160;m (8,040&#160;ft) respectively, whereas 12/30 remained at 1,300&#160;m (4,300&#160;ft). The civil aerodrome of Melsbroek was officially opened by <a href="/wiki/Prince_Charles,_Count_of_Flanders" title="Prince Charles, Count of Flanders">Prince Charles, Count of Flanders</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Regent" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Regent">Prince Regent</a>, on 20 July 1948. From 1948 to 1956 many more buildings and facilities were erected, mostly on the Melsbroek side of the site.\n</p><p>In 1955, a railway line from Brussels city centre to the airport was constructed. The line was officially opened by <a href="/wiki/Baudouin_I_of_Belgium" class="mw-redirect" title="Baudouin I of Belgium">King Baudouin</a> on 15 May 1955.\n</p><p>In 1956 a new 2,300&#160;m (7,500&#160;ft) runway was constructed, 07R/25L, which almost runs parallel with 07L/25R. The runway is still in use today and saw its length later increased to 3,200&#160;m (10,500&#160;ft). In April 1956 the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_federal_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Belgian federal government">Belgian government</a> decided to build a new airport, using the same runways, but with the buildings located within the municipality of Zaventem. In April 1957, construction started of the new terminal, preparing the airport for the <a href="/wiki/Expo_58" title="Expo 58">1958 World Fair</a>. The grass runway 12/30 had to make way to allow for the new passenger terminal. This new airport was inaugurated 5 July 1958, almost just in time for the 1958 World Fair. The buildings on the Melsbroek side are still in use by the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Air_Component" title="Belgian Air Component">Belgian Air Force</a> (<a href="/wiki/15th_Air_Transport_Wing" title="15th Air Transport Wing">15th Air Transport Wing</a>), and this is still known as Melsbroek airfield. Both <a href="/wiki/Zaventem_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Zaventem Airport">Zaventem Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melsbroek_Air_Base" title="Melsbroek Air Base">Melsbroek Air Base</a>, the military airfield, share the same runways.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_since_the_1960s">Development since the 1960s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Development since the 1960s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_707-329C,_Sabena_JP6848038.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Boeing_707-329C%2C_Sabena_JP6848038.jpg/220px-Boeing_707-329C%2C_Sabena_JP6848038.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Boeing_707-329C%2C_Sabena_JP6848038.jpg/330px-Boeing_707-329C%2C_Sabena_JP6848038.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Boeing_707-329C%2C_Sabena_JP6848038.jpg/440px-Boeing_707-329C%2C_Sabena_JP6848038.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="677" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_707-329C,_Sabena_JP6848038.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sabena" title="Sabena">Sabena</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_707-300" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 707-300">Boeing 707-300</a> at Brussels Airport in 1966</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10-30,_Air_Zaire_AN0199454.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10-30%2C_Air_Zaire_AN0199454.jpg/220px-McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10-30%2C_Air_Zaire_AN0199454.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10-30%2C_Air_Zaire_AN0199454.jpg/330px-McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10-30%2C_Air_Zaire_AN0199454.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10-30%2C_Air_Zaire_AN0199454.jpg/440px-McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10-30%2C_Air_Zaire_AN0199454.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="674" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10-30,_Air_Zaire_AN0199454.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Air_Za%C3%AFre" title="Air Za\xc3\xafre">Air Za\xc3\xafre</a> <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10" title="McDonnell Douglas DC-10">McDonnell Douglas DC-10</a> at Brussels Airport in 1990</div></div></div>\n<p>During the boom of commercial aviation in the 1960s and 1970s, several hangars were constructed. A new <a href="/wiki/Container_terminal" class="mw-redirect" title="Container terminal">cargo terminal</a> was constructed in 1976. In 1994, a brand new terminal was constructed adjacent to the old 1958 building. Two old piers were torn down and replaced by modern ones. In 2002, amidst the turmoil surrounding the demise of the national airline <a href="/wiki/Sabena" title="Sabena">Sabena</a>, a new pier was opened.\n</p><p>In 2005, the airport was awarded Best Airport in Europe by <a href="/wiki/Airports_Council_International" title="Airports Council International">Airports Council International</a>/<a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association" title="International Air Transport Association">International Air Transport Association</a> (ACI/IATA), based on a survey of over 100,000 passengers worldwide. Brussels Airport continued to appear in top airports lists as of 2012. A direct train link with <a href="/wiki/Leuven" title="Leuven">Leuven</a> and <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge" title="Li\xc3\xa8ge">Li\xc3\xa8ge</a> was opened on 12 December 2005.\n</p><p>In 2007, the airport served 17.8 million passengers, an increase of 7% over 2006. The cargo volume in the same year amounted to 780,000 tonnes, an increase of 8.9% over 2006. In 2008, the airport served 18.5 million passengers, which was an increase of 3.7% over the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sabena\'s demise meant a sharp fall in passenger traffic, a blow from which the airport only slowly recovered. The airport\'s future is threatened by disagreement between the governments of <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flanders</a> and the Brussels Capital Region concerning night-time air traffic routes.\n</p><p>In March 2009, the old mechanical <a href="/wiki/Flight_information_display_system" title="Flight information display system">Flight information display systems</a> were replaced by electronic ones.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> In September 2009, CEO Wilfried Van Assche resigned. One of the (unofficial) reasons was the delay in the construction of the low-cost terminal and the possible lawsuit by 52 airlines active at Brussels Airport, on the grounds of tax discrimination. It was Van Assche who started expanding the Long-Haul network (<a href="/wiki/Jet_Airways" title="Jet Airways">Jet Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hainan_Airlines" title="Hainan Airlines">Hainan Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/US_Airways" title="US Airways">US Airways</a>) at Brussels Airport. In February 2010 Arnaud Feist was appointed CEO. The Chairman of the Board is Marc Descheemaecker.\n</p>\n<ul><li>On 18 February 2013, in the <a href="/wiki/2013_Belgium_diamond_heist" class="mw-redirect" title="2013 Belgium diamond heist">2013 Belgium diamond heist</a>, eight men armed with automatic weapons and dressed in police uniforms seized 120 small parcels containing an estimated US$50 million worth of diamonds from a <a href="/wiki/Helvetic_Airways" title="Helvetic Airways">Helvetic Airways</a> <a href="/wiki/Fokker_100" title="Fokker 100">Fokker 100</a> passenger plane loaded with passengers preparing for departure to <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Z\xc3\xbcrich">Z\xc3\xbcrich</a>. The men drove two vehicles through a hole they had cut in the airport perimeter fence to Flight LX789, which had just been loaded with diamonds from a <a href="/wiki/Brink%27s" title="Brink&#39;s">Brink\'s</a> armored van from <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a>. They carried out the operation within five minutes with no injuries and without firing a shot.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>`</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016_Brussels_bombings">2016 Brussels bombings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2016 Brussels bombings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2016_Brussels_bombings" title="2016 Brussels bombings">2016 Brussels bombings</a></div>\n<p>On 22 March 2016, two explosions took place in Brussels Airport at 07:58 local time. One occurred near the <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airlines" title="Brussels Airlines">Brussels Airlines</a> check-in desks and the other next to a <a href="/wiki/Starbucks" title="Starbucks">Starbucks</a> coffee shop. A third bomb was found in the airport and detonated in a controlled explosion. The airport was closed after the attacks until 3 April, when it reopened with temporary facilities at less than 20% of its previous passenger capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg.com_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg.com-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Flights bound to Brussels Airport were either canceled or diverted to nearby airports such as <a href="/wiki/Brussels_South_Charleroi_Airport" title="Brussels South Charleroi Airport">Brussels South Charleroi Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ostend%E2%80%93Bruges_International_Airport" title="Ostend\xe2\x80\x93Bruges International Airport">Ostend\xe2\x80\x93Bruges International Airport</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">Schiphol</a>. At 09:11 <a href="/wiki/Central_European_Time" title="Central European Time">CET</a>, an explosion took place at <a href="/wiki/Maelbeek/Maalbeek_metro_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Maelbeek/Maalbeek metro station">Maelbeek/Maalbeek metro station</a>. <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">ISIL</a> claimed responsibility for the attacks as an act of revenge against <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> for participation in the ongoing <a href="/wiki/Military_intervention_against_ISIL" class="mw-redirect" title="Military intervention against ISIL">Military intervention against ISIL</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zaventem333.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Zaventem333.JPG/220px-Zaventem333.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zaventem333.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal exterior</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Moving_walkway_through_the_A-gates_of_Brussels_Airport_(DSCF7310).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Moving_walkway_through_the_A-gates_of_Brussels_Airport_%28DSCF7310%29.jpg/220px-Moving_walkway_through_the_A-gates_of_Brussels_Airport_%28DSCF7310%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" 2x" data-file-width="4875" data-file-height="3225" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Moving_walkway_through_the_A-gates_of_Brussels_Airport_(DSCF7310).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Departures area at Pier A</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussels_Airport_Runway_25_R.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Brussels_Airport_Runway_25_R.jpg/220px-Brussels_Airport_Runway_25_R.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Brussels_Airport_Runway_25_R.jpg/330px-Brussels_Airport_Runway_25_R.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Brussels_Airport_Runway_25_R.jpg/440px-Brussels_Airport_Runway_25_R.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2778" data-file-height="1511" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussels_Airport_Runway_25_R.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Runway and apron</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Controletoren_Brussel-Nationaal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Controletoren_Brussel-Nationaal.jpg/220px-Controletoren_Brussel-Nationaal.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Controletoren_Brussel-Nationaal.jpg/330px-Controletoren_Brussel-Nationaal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Controletoren_Brussel-Nationaal.jpg/440px-Controletoren_Brussel-Nationaal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2528" data-file-height="1685" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Controletoren_Brussel-Nationaal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Control tower</div></div></div>\n<p>Brussels Airport uses a one terminal concept, meaning that all the facilities are located under a single roof. The terminal building consists of several levels. The <a href="/wiki/Brussels_National_Airport_railway_station" title="Brussels National Airport railway station">railway station</a> is located on \xe2\x88\x921, buses and taxis arrive at 0, arrivals are located on level 2 and departures on level 3. Levels 2 and 3 are connected to the airport\'s two piers (A and B).<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pier_A">Pier A</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Pier A">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Pier A is the newest pier on Brussels Airport and was opened on 15 May 2002. This pier was destined to support flights from and to the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen</a> countries (A-gates). However, since 15 October 2008 all <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airlines" title="Brussels Airlines">Brussels Airlines</a> flights to African destinations are also handled at this pier. Therefore, border control was installed towards the end of the pier in order to create a new pier. As a result, gates A61-72 were renamed T61-72. Later, Brussels Airlines\' daily flight to New York was also moved here from pier B.\n</p><p>Until 26 March 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Pier A was connected to the main building via a 400-metre-long (1,300&#160;ft) tunnel under the apron. Each pier used to have its own security zone, so transfer between the piers involved a security check, which for practical purposes made it to be two terminals. This tunnel was replaced by the "Connector", a new building that links both piers above ground and allows passengers to walk straight from the check-in desk to their gate in pier A or B, without changing floors. In the opposite direction, the building provides arriving passengers with a smooth and convenient passage to the baggage reclaim hall and the exit. Furthermore, border control has been relocated behind the 25-lane screening platform (Europe\'s largest) inside the Connector which means that changing planes no longer requires a security check.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pier_B">Pier B</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Pier B">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Pier B is the oldest pier still in use at Brussels Airport and is only used for flights outside the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>. Pier B is connected immediately to the main departure hall and consists of two decks. The upper deck (level 3) is at the same level as the departure halls and is used for the departing passengers, whereas the lower deck (level 2) is used for arriving passengers and connects immediately to border control and the <a href="/wiki/Baggage_claim" class="mw-redirect" title="Baggage claim">baggage claim area</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Planned">Planned</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Planned">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pier_A_West">Pier A West</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Pier A West">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Pier A West is a planned expansion of Pier A, and is meant to relieve Pier B by also handling flights from non-<a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen</a> countries. Pier A West was due to open in 2016, but because of the slow passenger growth, Brussels Airport announced in July 2013 that the works would be delayed. However, in November 2015, Brussels Airport announced a major 550 million euro investment and pointed out that within this investment the extension of the pier is included.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Low-cost_pier">Low-cost pier</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Low-cost pier">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Just as is the case for Pier A West, the construction of a new <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost</a> pier is currently on hold. It will be built roughly where the old south pier used to be. At present, several low-cost airlines including <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a> fly to <a href="/wiki/Charleroi_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Charleroi Airport">Brussels-South Charleroi Airport</a>, 40&#160;km (25&#160;mi) away from Brussels.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In autumn 2013, low-cost carrier <a href="/wiki/Pegasus_Airlines" title="Pegasus Airlines">Pegasus Airlines</a> announced it would end its flights between Brussels Airport and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>. The service between Brussels and <a href="/wiki/Sabiha_G%C3%B6k%C3%A7en_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Sabiha G\xc3\xb6k\xc3\xa7en International Airport">Istanbul\xe2\x80\x93Sabiha G\xc3\xb6k\xc3\xa7en</a> would relocate to Brussels-South Charleroi Airport. However, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">Turkish Airlines</a> announced on 26 November 2013 it would offer one daily flight on the same route, starting one month after Pegasus terminated its operations at the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-airlineroute.net_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airlineroute.net-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> One day later, Ryanair announced the opening of a second Belgian base at Brussels Airport, giving a boost to low-cost traffic at Brussels Airport. Ryanair announced on 27 November 10 new routes from Brussels Airport,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> although Brussels-South Charleroi Airport will remain the low-cost carrier\'s primary Belgian base.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Shops, bars and restaurants are scattered throughout the building. A few facilities are located in the departure area. These are mostly convenience stores and small shops such as the airport shop, a pharmacy, <a href="/wiki/Relay_(shop)" title="Relay (shop)">Relay</a> stores and a coffee shop. But most of the facilities can only be accessed after Security control \xe2\x80\x93and are tax free. Several brands and chains have a branch in both piers, however several only operate in pier A. The airport also features places of worship (for <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestants">Protestants</a>), as well as a place for meditation for <a href="/wiki/Humanism" title="Humanism">humanists</a>. The airport provides meeting facilities and can host congresses up to 600 participants, either in the Regus Skyport Meeting Center or in the <a href="/wiki/Sheraton_Hotels_and_Resorts" title="Sheraton Hotels and Resorts">Sheraton</a> Brussels Airport Hotel. The latter is the only hotel located on the airport grounds, opposite the terminal. Shuttle services are provided to 14 nearby hotels.\n</p><p>All passengers now have unlimited free Wi-Fi access.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There is a small smoking room next to gate A67 in the transfer section of pier A.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_facilities">Other facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Other facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Several airlines have or had its head offices at the grounds of Brussels Airport. <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airlines" title="Brussels Airlines">Brussels Airlines</a> has its corporate head office in the b.house, Airport Building 26, located in <a href="/wiki/Diegem" title="Diegem">Diegem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machelen" title="Machelen">Machelen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Machmap_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Machmap-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/European_Air_Transport" class="mw-redirect" title="European Air Transport">European Air Transport</a> had its head office in Building 4\xe2\x80\x935, in <a href="/wiki/Zaventem" title="Zaventem">Zaventem</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Before <a href="/wiki/Sabena" title="Sabena">Sabena</a> went out of business, its head office was in the Sabena House on the grounds of Brussels Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> When it existed, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Express" title="Virgin Express">Virgin Express</a> had its head office in Building 116 in Zaventem.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/SN_Brussels" class="mw-redirect" title="SN Brussels">SN Brussels</a>, which formed in 2002, had its head office in Airport Building 117 in Zaventem when it existed.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Prior to its disestablishment, <a href="/wiki/Sobelair" title="Sobelair">Sobelair</a> had its head office in Building 45 in Zaventem.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/CityBird" title="CityBird">CityBird</a> was based in building 117D.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The cargo airline <a href="/wiki/Cargo_B_Airlines" title="Cargo B Airlines">Cargo B Airlines</a> had its head office in the Brucarco Building 706 in Zaventem.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger">Passenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Passenger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following airlines operate regular scheduled and charter flights to and from Brussels:<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="font-size:95%"><tbody><tr><th>Airlines</th><th class="unsortable">Destinations</th></tr><tr><td><a <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki_Airport" title="Thessaloniki Airport">Thessaloniki</a>\n</td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">Aer Lingus</a> </td><td> <a Airport">Montr\xc3\xa9al\xe2\x80\x93Trudeau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Pearson_International_Airport" title="Toronto Pearson International Airport">Toronto\xe2\x80\x93Pearson</a>\n</td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Air_Europa" title="Air Europa">Air Europa</a> </td><td> <a href="/wiki/Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport" style="text-align:center;">\n<th>1993\n</th>\n<td>10,000,000+</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93</td>\n<td></td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="text-align:center;">\n<th>1950\n</th>\n<td>240,000+</td>\n<td>\xe2\x80\x93</td>\n<td></td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<ul><li>The relapse in 2001 and 2002 is due to the combined effects of the <a href="/wiki/September_11_Attacks" class="mw-redirect" title="September 11 Attacks">September 11 Attacks</a> and the collapse of then home carrier <a href="/wiki/Sabena" title="Sabena">Sabena</a> in the final quarter of 2001.</li>\n<li>The Cargo relapse in 2008 and 2009 is due to the combined effects of the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x9308">Financial crisis of 2007\xe2\x80\x9308</a>, also affecting passenger volumes in 2009, and the relocation of <a href="/wiki/DHL_Aviation" title="DHL Aviation">DHL Aviation</a> to <a href="/wiki/Leipzig/Halle_Airport" title="Leipzig/Halle Airport">Leipzig/Halle Airport</a>. DHL departed after the Belgian government decided they couldn\'t operate more cargo flights at night because of noise for the people living in the surrounding area.</li>\n<li>The 2016 decrease in passenger numbers and aircraft movements results from the <a href="/wiki/2016_Brussels_bombings" title="2016 Brussels bombings">2016 Brussels bombings</a> which caused the airport to close for 11 days before reopening with severely reduced capacity.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Routes">Routes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Ground transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:START-lijn_272_Brussels_Airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/START-lijn_272_Brussels_Airport.jpg/220px-START-lijn_272_Brussels_Airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/START-lijn_272_Brussels_Airport.jpg/330px-START-lijn_272_Brussels_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/START-lijn_272_Brussels_Airport.jpg/440px-START-lijn_272_Brussels_Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1238" data-file-height="1120" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:START-lijn_272_Brussels_Airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Brussels Airport bus service</div></div></div>\n<p>Brussels Airport can be reached by car via the A201, which is directly connected to the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Ring" title="Brussels Ring">Brussels Ring Road</a>. From there, the main <a href="/wiki/List_of_motorways_in_Belgium" title="List of motorways in Belgium">highways of Belgium</a> can directly be accessed. Private partners provide three car parks at the airport, offering in total 10,600 parking spaces. <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Shell</a> operates a self-service <a href="/wiki/Filling_station" title="Filling station">gas station</a> near the exit of the airport complex.\n</p><p>Several car rental services are located in the airport as well. <a href="/wiki/Europcar" title="Europcar">Europcar</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Hertz_Corporation" title="The Hertz Corporation">Hertz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sixt" title="Sixt">Sixt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dollar_Thrifty_Automotive_Group" title="Dollar Thrifty Automotive Group">Thrifty</a> all operate at Brussels Airport. <a href="/wiki/DriveNow" title="DriveNow">DriveNow</a> also offers a car-sharing service at Brussels airport located at P3 Holiday Parking,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> and Zipcar has parking spaces.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Taxi2Share provides sharing cab service from airport.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/De_Lijn" title="De Lijn">De Lijn</a> provides bus transportation to and from various cities in Flanders from platforms A and B (via <a href="/wiki/Brucargo" class="mw-redirect" title="Brucargo">Brucargo</a>). The <a href="/wiki/MIVB" class="mw-redirect" title="MIVB">MIVB</a>/STIB provides transportation into Brussels city centre from Schuman railway station, <a href="/wiki/Brussels-Luxembourg_railway_station" title="Brussels-Luxembourg railway station">Brussels Luxembourg Station</a> and Tr\xc3\xb4ne Metro Station via line 12 from platform C. Platform E is used by the Hotel Shuttles, offering shuttle services to several hotels near the area.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Taxi" class="mw-redirect" title="Taxi">Taxis</a> are permanently available in front of the arrivals hall. Licensed taxis can be recognized by the blue and yellow emblem.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airport_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Brussels Airport railway station">Brussels Airport railway station</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussels_Airport_Railway_Station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Brussels_Airport_Railway_Station.jpg/220px-Brussels_Airport_Railway_Station.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Brussels_Airport_Railway_Station.jpg/330px-Brussels_Airport_Railway_Station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Brussels_Airport_Railway_Station.jpg/440px-Brussels_Airport_Railway_Station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brussels_Airport_Railway_Station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Brussels_National_Airport_railway_station" title="Brussels National Airport railway station">Brussels National Airport railway station</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Brussels_National_Airport_railway_station" title="Brussels National Airport railway station">Airport Railway Station</a> is located under the airport building at level \xe2\x88\x921. The train station has direct services to <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a>, Brussels, <a href="/wiki/De_Panne" title="De Panne">De Panne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghent" title="Ghent">Ghent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hasselt" title="Hasselt">Hasselt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Landen" title="Landen">Landen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leuven" title="Leuven">Leuven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mechelen" title="Mechelen">Mechelen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nivelles" title="Nivelles">Nivelles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qu%C3%A9vy" title="Qu\xc3\xa9vy">Qu\xc3\xa9vy</a>. At least four trains per hour serve the most used link to <a href="/wiki/Brussels-South_railway_station" title="Brussels-South railway station">Brussels South Railway Station</a>, where international connections are offered by <a href="/wiki/Eurostar" title="Eurostar">Eurostar</a> (to London), <a href="/wiki/Thalys" title="Thalys">Thalys</a> (to <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Avignon" title="Avignon">Avignon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Essen" title="Essen">Essen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lille" title="Lille">Lille</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a>, Paris and <a href="/wiki/Valence,_Dr%C3%B4me" title="Valence, Dr\xc3\xb4me">Valence</a>), <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" class="mw-redirect" title="Intercity-Express">ICE</a> (to <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Eurocity" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurocity">Eurocity</a> (to <a href="/wiki/Basel" title="Basel">Basel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bern" title="Bern">Bern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chur" title="Chur">Chur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Z\xc3\xbcrich">Z\xc3\xbcrich</a>).\n</p><p>A direct train link with Leuven was opened on 12 December 2005. A direct link with <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mechelen" title="Mechelen">Mechelen</a> via the so-called <a href="/wiki/Diabolo_project" title="Diabolo project">Diabolo</a> line was opened for public service on 10 June 2012. The Diabolo project is a <a href="/wiki/Public-private_partnership" class="mw-redirect" title="Public-private partnership">public-private partnership</a>. It has been decided that all rail passengers to the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_National_Airport_railway_station" title="Brussels National Airport railway station">Brussels National Airport railway station</a> pay a "Diabolo supplement" to finance the ongoing and planned work.\n</p><p>As of December 2014, a direct train link between <a href="/wiki/Bruges" title="Bruges">Bruges</a> and the Airport will be offered,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> just as an Intercity service to <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">Schiphol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since the new <a href="/wiki/Schuman-Josaphat_tunnel" title="Schuman-Josaphat tunnel">Schuman-Josaphat tunnel</a><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> has been finished, a new connection has been established to connect Brussels Airport directly to the stations of the EU quarter, being <a href="/wiki/Schuman_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Schuman station">Brussels-Schuman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brussels-Luxembourg_railway_station" title="Brussels-Luxembourg railway station">Brussels-Luxembourg</a>. This brought the travel time between the Airport and the EU quarter to 15 minutes. The Belgian Railways announced the line to open as an hourly service.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> However, the line now sees a train every 30 minutes on weekdays.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tram">Tram</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Tram">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In an attempt to alleviate gridlock around Brussels, the Flemish regional transport company <a href="/wiki/De_Lijn" title="De Lijn">De Lijn</a> started the Brabantnet project, which was scheduled to be finished by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\nThree new light rail lines will be created, of which 2 will terminate at Brussels Airport:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The Airport Tram, connecting Brussels Airport to <a href="/wiki/Brussels-North_railway_station" title="Brussels-North railway station">Brussels-North</a>, but taking a different trajectory from the existing railway line;</li>\n<li>The Ring Tram, roughly following the northern side of the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Ring" title="Brussels Ring">Brussels Ring</a> and connecting several Brussels suburbs and Vilvoorde to the Airport.</li></ul>\n<p>To speed up the process, testing started in August 2016 with a Trambus, a <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">Bus rapid transit</a> system developed by Belgian bus builder <a href="/wiki/Van_Hool" title="Van Hool">Van Hool</a>, which requires less investment than a tram.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Ringtrambus</i> started service on 28 July 2020, using 14 24-metre double-articulated buses. The initial half-hourly service is to be upgraded to quarter-hourly on 1 September 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Route 820 runs between Brussels Airport and the Brussels University Hospital in Jette, via Brucargo, the station and the centre of Vilvoorde, the Kassei neighbourhood, the employment area around the Medialaan, Strombeek and the Heysel. This solution is presented as an in-between step until the tram line is finished.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Airport Tram will be an extension of present <a href="/wiki/Brussels_tram_route_55" title="Brussels tram route 55">Brussels Tram line 55</a> and line 62,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> and will roughly follow the <a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autoroute_A201_(Belgique)" class="extiw" title="fr:Autoroute A201 (Belgique)">A201 Motorway</a>, but will need a large bridge to cross the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Ring" title="Brussels Ring">Brussels Ring</a> into the Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bicycle">Bicycle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Bicycle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Brussels Airport has a special separated road that provides access to the airport for bikers and pedestrians. There is also a special place to park bikes. Since 2019, the airport has a direct connection from the Bike Highway <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Leuven" title="Leuven">Leuven</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, merely 1% of employees were commuting by bike.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In an effort to further increase this number, bicycle leasing was introduced to employees, and in 2020 almost 10% of the Brussels Airport employees signed up for this.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_747_crash_bxl.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Boeing_747_crash_bxl.jpg/220px-Boeing_747_crash_bxl.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Boeing_747_crash_bxl.jpg/330px-Boeing_747_crash_bxl.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Boeing_747_crash_bxl.jpg/440px-Boeing_747_crash_bxl.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_747_crash_bxl.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a> that overran the runway in 2008</div></div></div>\n<ul><li>On 15 February 1961, <a href="/wiki/Sabena_Flight_548" title="Sabena Flight 548">Sabena Flight 548</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_707" title="Boeing 707">Boeing 707</a>, crashed during <a href="/wiki/Final_approach_(aviation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Final approach (aviation)">approach</a> on runway 20, killing all 72 people on board and one on the ground.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> This was the first fatal accident involving a Boeing 707, resulting in the death of the entire <a href="/wiki/U.S._Figure_Skating" title="U.S. Figure Skating">United States Figure Skating</a> team on its way to the <a href="/wiki/World_Figure_Skating_Championships" title="World Figure Skating Championships">World Figure Skating Championships</a> in Prague, Czechoslovakia, which the <a href="/wiki/International_Skating_Union" title="International Skating Union">International Skating Union</a> subsequently cancelled out of respect for the team.</li>\n<li>Four aircraft were destroyed on 5 May 2006 when Sabena Technics\' <a href="/wiki/Hangar" title="Hangar">hangar</a> 40 burned down. The aircraft were one <a href="/wiki/C-130_Hercules" class="mw-redirect" title="C-130 Hercules">Lockheed C-130 Hercules</a> (Belgian Air Component) and three <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A-320" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A-320">Airbus A320</a> (<a href="/wiki/Armavia" title="Armavia">Armavia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenian_International_Airways" title="Armenian International Airways">Armenian International Airways</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hellas_Jet" title="Hellas Jet">Hellas Jet</a>).</li>\n<li>On 25 May 2008, <a href="/wiki/Kalitta_Air" title="Kalitta Air">Kalitta Air</a> Flight 207, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747-200F</a>, overran the shorter runway 20, crashed into a field and split in three. Four of the five people on board received minor injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brussels_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Belgium" title="Transport in Belgium">Transport in Belgium</a></li></ul>\n<div style="clear:right;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
